<name>Nick Kisling</name><Date>1558393930735<//Date>< rating>
3<//rating>
<Text>When I moved here a year ago I found this place on accident on my bicycle via the bridge to nowhere. Which is actually pretty cool....not sure why they would build a bridge that dead ends. The hike itself is nothing special, its pretty moderate...unless you want to walk the entire preserve than that would be intense. Nice and quiet though and after all the rains lots of flowers. No bikes or dogs allowed which is cool for the snakes and bunnies and whatnot that live there. After these rains it would be a good place to go herpin for snakes and lizards. Here are the directions if you want to come in from the direction instead of the normal way.
San Marcos Foothills Preserve is located at 1083 Via Gaitero, Santa Barbara CA 93105.
From Highway 101, take Highway 154 San Marcos Pass. Exit at Cathedral Oaks Rd and turn left. Turn right on Via Chaparral. After half a block, on your right you see a bridge, the Bridge to Nowhere. Cross it- it goes over Highway 154. Then turn left and park along the road.< /Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>

Our move was about as far as one can go in the US (coast to coast), exactly 3000 miles. We did a ton of research to weigh all of the options in terms of reputable movers and cost‚Äîbetter business bureau, reviews online (multiple places like Yelp, Google, mymovingreviews), advice from friends, AAA, etc. We decided to go with Moving Pros for a variety of reasons, the main ones being a competitive price, professional service upfront with the estimate on site, professional service in terms of phone calls and written estimate by email, reviews, and a ‚Äúlive load‚Äù moving promise (this means they pack the stuff into a truck and it is not stored in a warehouse but driven directly to its destination).

Overall, things turned out really well, and we had high expectations. They arrived on the day they said they would and it was delivered on time, on our preferred date. Especially on the California end, where Moving Pro is located, they were amazing. The owner himself (Haim) was there to pack and load with a large crew and they really did a great job of organizing the pack and loading of the truck. First class! They took the time to pay attention to the details in terms of the pack, and ensure that our home was protected from damage. Everything went perfectly. This says a lot since it was a 3000 sq ft home with a large (and full) three car garage. They came with seven guys, which was impressive.

It's hard to decide on a mover, but we're happy with Moving Pros overall, especially the professional and personalized service we received from the owners, Vicky and Haim. 5 Stars.</review>

An inexpensive dresser did get damaged in the long-distance (3,000 mi) transport. MovingPros reimbursed me the cost of the dresser with no hassles. One area of improvement: I wish they would have given me tips about how to pack boxes for long-distance moves. Nothing was damaged in the boxes but they came across 3,000 mi pretty beat up. Next time I'd go with reinforced (and more expensive) boxes for such a long-distance move. But overall, I'm very pleased with my experience with MovingPros.< /text>

<userid>104390479400303772939<//userid><resp>None<//resp><rate>4<//rate>< Review>
Small and simple and easy to get to. Close to the LAX Airport. They offer shuttle service to the airport. Small pool with bathrooms and a sitting area to eat close by. The back of the motel has a Greek restaurant so if you are hungry and don't have a car you can walk right to it from the motel. There are drinks and coffee and a pancake service machine in the front office.
Of course it's an older building, but they did update the rooms to give you a clean fresh modern look. Not sure how loud it is at night, didn't spend the night, just a quick visit to see the area.< /Review>

I'm giving 5 stars for two reasons: the room was immaculate and the bed was very comfortable!  Keep in mind you are only 1 mile from the airport and jets are flying over the motel. <GmapID>0x80c2b729bf300d57:0xe8b2e4d4861f040b< /GmapID><Resp>None<//Resp>< Review>
The motel is located about 2.5 km from the airport. Every minute or so there's a plane flying almost above your head. Fortunately, the noise isn't that bad when inside the room. The surroundings aren't really interesting.
The room is clean has a big, comfortable bed. It's equipped with an ironing board, iron, flat-screen TV with cable, quite big fridge, mini coffee machine. The bathroom is clean. You get towels, free toiletries and a hair dryer. The room is much better than the overall look and feel of the motel (which is average). The staff is rather nice and helpful. They have a swimming pool but I didn't have a chance to use it.
Breakfast is mediocre. But the add-water-and-stir oatmeal and coffee weren't bad.
Overall impression - a decent place for one or two nights, especially when you travel for several hours and you want sth close to the airport, with a comfortable bed.</Review>

< Text>
The motel is located about 2.5 km from the airport. Every minute or so there's a plane flying almost above your head. Fortunately, the noise isn't that bad when inside the room. The surroundings aren't really interesting.
The room is clean has a big, comfortable bed. It's equipped with an ironing board, iron, flat-screen TV with cable, quite big fridge, mini coffee machine. The bathroom is clean. You get towels, free toiletries and a hair dryer. The room is much better than the overall look and feel of the motel (which is average). The staff is rather nice and helpful. They have a swimming pool but I didn't have a chance to use it.
Breakfast is mediocre. But the add-water-and-stir oatmeal and coffee weren't bad.
Overall impression - a decent place for one or two nights, especially when you travel for several hours and you want sth close to the airport, with a comfortable bed.<//Text>

< text>
This establishment has the very dangerous practice of making a paper copy of your credit card with all information exposed (all 16 numbers, expiration date and your full name) plus your driver's license number on the registration form you sign at check in.
Upon checkout instead of giving me back that paper with all my info as I requested they give me a printed receipt showing only the last 4 numbers of the credit card.
I explained to the manager that it should be the other way around; I'm the one who is supposed to have the copy with all my info and they keep the the info with the last 4 digits of the credit card as every other hotel does but she refused.
I asked the manager to at least black out all numbers of the credit card copy except the last 4 numbers just like the receipt they gave me but the she refused, stating that it is their practice to keep a PAPER COPY of ALL credit card info and driver's license number of each guest that stay there.
I pointed out to the manager that whoever has that paper copy can easily pretend to be me, that it blantenly creates a great opportunity for credit card fraud / identity theft.
Her only answer to that was that it is the way they do business. My response to her was that making a complete copy of the credit card for a purchase was the way things were done back in 1970's and for very good reason that practice has ended - with the exception of her hotel.
This was a life lesson of you get what you pay for; I should have stayed at a hotel that cost twice as much and saved myself this heasdache.
Now I have to go through the hell of getting a new credit card / number from my bank.<//text>

<Review>I only stayed here for one night last week and I'll just break it down into the pros and cons below.

Pros:
-Room was very clean and nice size by motel standards
-Location is great as it's practically within walking distance of the airport
-Vending machines were stocked with snacks and drinks at reasonable prices
-No bugs
-The young man in his 20's or 30's behind the counter (latino man) was polite.

Cons:
-Due to it's close proximity to the airport you can hear planes flying overhead all night. Out of all motels and hotels in the area, this is the one that probably has the most amount of noise from planes due to it's position to the runway. I'm an extremely light sleeper but it wasn't bad enough to where I lost sleep and not really something the hotel owners can control so this isn't really a con I guess but should be noted for others.

-The "free breakfast" in the morning was my biggest irk with this place. I went down there and saw people making their own waffles and eggs and things instead of having it all there on a table. I mean they seriously have customers using a waffle griddle to make their own waffles. I just had cereal because I know nothing about these things or how to use them and don't want to look/feel dumb for asking. Most hotels/motels that offer free breakfast put plates out with waffles, eggs, etc. and you just use tongs and spoons to scoop them out of the plates on the table and onto your plate. Not cool having people wake up that early to be greeted with the same work they'd have to do in their own kitchen at home.

-The lady behind the counter was not the friendliest. I don't know what her issue was but she seemed to be in a bad mood and after I paid her, the younger gentleman sort of took over explaining a few things. He may have noticed she was in a bad mood too possibly. I'm a pretty timid and quiet type person, not aggressive at all so I don't feel it was me who put her in a bad mood and I don't feel anything I said or did triggered her bad mood. She did get smart with me/snippy at one thing with me out of nowhere. There's a sign on the counter which states "No debit cards accepted" which is a con in itself and absolutely ridiculous, so I just stated "oh I didn't know I couldn't pay with a debit card, can I go to an ATM real quick to get cash. I booked the room online through a discount site and she goes "You already paid through the website. If I needed your card I would have asked for it already". I'm not a noob at traveling and there's been many times where I've booked a room online and then had to actually make payment once there. The credit card online is sometimes just to reserve a room, not to actually make the payment. The attitude was completely unnecessary as it was a simple friendly question.

-At the time I was there they were not accepting debit cards for payment.

-The front desk lady put a piece of paper in front of me that said "special discount rate" and it showed the hotel room was about $10 cheaper on that piece of paper than what I paid on the discount website. So this of course got me wondering if this was their deal with the hotel, or if that was the price I would have paid if I had gone through the hotel directly and not the third-party "discount site" online. While this may have just been a special deal with the third-party company and didn't really mean I was overcharged by the discount site, I still should not have seen that paper because that gets the wheels turning in people's heads and makes them start wondering if they just lost $10 or not. She put the paper in front of me to write something on it, not necessarily to show me the paper, but it was quite obvious what it said as she laid on the table facing me for a few seconds, probably not paying attention to what she did and I glanced at it thinking maybe it was my receipt or something I had to sign.

-I walked to this hotel from the airport area but noticed that for people who are driving, there's no space in the tiny parking lot. There were literally a few cars parked behind other cars boxing them in.<//Review><rating>4< /rating>< resp>
